    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_2664531745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2664531745" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1362506-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442472304p2/1362506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2664531745?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/1362506-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2664531745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4802692074183507607">‘You’re in the grip of death fear. I have the same thing, death fear.’<br/><br/>British author J (for Johnny) Jupes falls into that fascinating world of unclassifiable authors: his genre embraces mystery (as suggested by his series designator ‘The Detectives That Don’t Fit’) and humor and off the wall verbiage that is a pure delight to read. According to Jupes, he writes ‘pulp and dystopian novels and likes having a cover image in front of him before even thinking about the first word. Raised by a strict </span>
  <span id="freeText4802692074183507607" style="display:none">‘You’re in the grip of death fear. I have the same thing, death fear.’<br /><br />British author J (for Johnny) Jupes falls into that fascinating world of unclassifiable authors: his genre embraces mystery (as suggested by his series designator ‘The Detectives That Don’t Fit’) and humor and off the wall verbiage that is a pure delight to read. According to Jupes, he writes ‘pulp and dystopian novels and likes having a cover image in front of him before even thinking about the first word. Raised by a strict English playwright, Jupes can't stomach convention.’ And to say more would distract form the experience of reading his well-crafted novel HAIRSPRAY AND LIGHTER. <br /><br />Yes there is a story amidst all the wild writing but it takes a bit to crawl into the tunnel of words and once acclimated to the writing style the story gains impact. For starters, the opening language is as follows: ‘Dawn yielded, flooding west over Houston like blood backtracking into the gray dope filling that morning’s syringe. Trap Boy stood, frozen, arm raised, mouth open, a prehistoric peat man, until the blue and white Volare made its turn onto B and everything began to move, him cawing No-Joke, No-Joke, No-Joke, the other mad hatters joining in, all of them trolling the east side between 2nd and 3rd. The car’s windows were rolled down. Two blueberries slumped in their seats, staring ahead, listening to brand names, Cash, Chinatown, Poison, echo through gutted space. Something was happening that wouldn’t happen again; the air was torn, and no one had a clue what just spilled out the gash; the city, a rat’s whisker away from shattering. The RMP cut across the next intersection; a few feet over on 4th, bucket hats, hoodies, Adidas, all lined up behind the jagged hole sledge hammered through a bombed-up cinder block wall. Framed inside was the head of Benji, fourteen, price tag swinging off the side of his Knick’s cap. Benji handed a glassine envelope to a man in a wheel chair, the line nudged forward. Next block, a torn tan polyester suit pushed his way out two cracked glass double doors reflecting the RMP’s skewed white stripe, frosted red bulb over the frame making it for after-hours. The suit spun, plastered, already falling, fell, flat on his face; the officers catching salsa pop before the doors pulled shut. Then a sloppy fist fight, nothing serious; and on that corner, a single soul was tilted, a hand floating in front of his face, eyes closed. The smell of coffee and fresh bagels blew through the car before it made a right onto 14th; slowing in front of a sooty walk-up, sandwiched between two other sooty walk ups. The driver lit his last Chesterfield of the shift.’<br /><br />So where does this take us? To an ingenious murder story that focuses on hairspray and <br />butane lighter. Or as the synopsis suggests, ‘All Detective Eckerly wanted to do that day was place a bet on a horse. He didn't expect Darlene Johnson to walk into his office with her chocolate box. And certainly didn't expect what followed. . .<br /><br />Once adjusted to the writing style Jupes is refreshingly different. Let’s see where he will take us next! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4802692074183507607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2683468337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2683468337" />
    <a title="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez"><img alt="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467911475p2/56536968.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2683468337?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez" href="/user/show/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez">Luis Humberto Molinar Márquez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56536968-luis-humberto-molinar-m-rquez?shelf=randr">randr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2683468337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9453193247796490090">English Review + Reseña en Español.<br/><br/>Hairspray and Lighter, by Johnny “J.” Jupes (144 pages, published by Hekate Publishing, 2018), is the first part of the “High Heels and Hemorroids”, also known as “The Detectives That Don’t Fit” series, and is a hard-boiled, private investigator / muder mistery noir thriller.<br/><br/>An assassin is running loose with a can of aerosol hairspray, a lighter and some accounts to collect. A private detective wakes up in his apartment after a game of poker, with the intention</span>
  <span id="freeText9453193247796490090" style="display:none">English Review + Reseña en Español.<br /><br />Hairspray and Lighter, by Johnny “J.” Jupes (144 pages, published by Hekate Publishing, 2018), is the first part of the “High Heels and Hemorroids”, also known as “The Detectives That Don’t Fit” series, and is a hard-boiled, private investigator / muder mistery noir thriller.<br /><br />An assassin is running loose with a can of aerosol hairspray, a lighter and some accounts to collect. A private detective wakes up in his apartment after a game of poker, with the intention of going to the horse races to bet. An exotic diamond has been stolen and a blonde with asymmetrical breasts and a box of chocolates needs a hand.<br /><br />A couple of days are enough to develop the dark, bloody and mysterious plot of Hairspray and Lighter. Starting from a simple noir premise, the story gets complicated when private detective Eckerly, his poker buddies, a poet in love and an elderly cat lover are dragged into a violent vortex stained with theft, kidnapping, rape, death, people trafficking and mad scientists.<br />This novel is well written, the characters have sufficient dimension, the story develops with agility and the plot has a good endowment of mystery.<br />I enjoyed reading this rather short novel.<br /><br />-----<br /><br />Hairspray and Lighter, de Johnny "J." Jupes (144 páginas, publicada por Hekate Publishing, 2018), es la primera parte de "Tacones Altos y Hemorroides", también conocida como la serie "Los detectives que no encajan", y es una novela de suspenso negro, detectives privados, misterio de asesinato y trata.<br /><br />Una asesina anda suelta con una lata de fijador en aerosol, un encendedor y algunas cuentas por cobrar. Un detective privado despierta en su departamento después de un juego de póker, con la intención de ir al hipódromo a apostar. Un diamante exótico ha sido robado y una rubia con senos asimétricos y una caja de chocolates necesita una mano.<br /><br />Bastan un par de días para desarrollar la trama oscura, sangrienta y misteriosa de Hairspray and Lighter. Partiendo de una premisa noir simple, la historia se complica cuando el detective privado Eckerly, sus compañeros de póker, una poetisa enamorada y una anciana amante de los gatos se vean arrastrados hacia una vorágine violenta manchada de robo, secuestro, violación, muerte, tráfico de personas y científicos locos. Esta novela está bien escrita, los personajes tienen suficiente dimensión, la historia se desarrolla con agilidad y la trama cuenta con una buena dotación de misterio.<br /><br />Disfruté leyendo esta novela más bien corta. La trama es interesante y los personajes bastante simpáticos, además de que toca temas escabrosos de la vida real.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9453193247796490090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4913692647582442564">First things first: this is a quick read that’s well worth the couple of hours of your time. I am a huge fan of books with somber and/or dark undertones, and this book hits the “jackpot” section in that regard. Throw in a dash of unique style and we have ourselves a book that really pushes the genre, reinventing the style that we don’t see in many books these days.   <span id="freeText4913692647582442564" style="display:none">First things first: this is a quick read that’s well worth the couple of hours of your time. I am a huge fan of books with somber and/or dark undertones, and this book hits the “jackpot” section in that regard. Throw in a dash of unique style and we have ourselves a book that really pushes the genre, reinventing the style that we don’t see in many books these days. The author took a (likely calculated) risk with this story /formatting and writing style, and I think it paid off pretty well.<br />The story follows Eckerly (a cop) tracking a string of homicides with an interesting trend/connection. There are twists (some of which aren’t entirely unpredictable), and some unusual (not unusual in a bad way) plot points, but you know what? The writing was so unique and calculated that it made everything work well even if it was done in an unconventional style for a noir tale. I actually couldn’t stop reading once I started. The pace and flow worked well, and it was easy to get absorbed in the excitement of it all.</span>

  <span id="freeText12766872367974462372" style="display:none">To say that Hairspray and Lighter (The Detectives That Don't Fit Book 1) by J. Jupes is an offbeat kind of book is an understatement. The format, the language, and most of all the story is unique and presents a reading challenge. This is a noir detective story featuring a hard boiled detective in Detective Eckerly, not your typical detective and not an ordinary character. The writing is fast paced, kind of crazy in spots, but deep under the surface of the clutter is a good story, a story which focuses on the modus operandi of you guessed it, hairspray and a lighter. A solid murder mystery with impressive, shocking language and writing that takes a bit of adjusting to, you will need to settle in and pay attention as this story unfolds. Not for the faint of heart, this tale is highly recommended for a unique and unsettling reading experience. </span>

  <span id="freeText3200706752279482648" style="display:none">Jupes isn’t a writer I was previously aware of, and as the book cover is rather odd I wasn’t sure what to expect inside. <div id="review_2741781587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2741781587" />
    <a title="Rabid Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74063500-rabid-reads"><img alt="Rabid Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533567274p2/74063500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741781587?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rabid Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rabid Reads" href="/user/show/74063500-rabid-reads">Rabid Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741781587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8913011632799117643">Hairspray and Lighter is a dark and broody, gritty, noir read. It strayed off the beaten path of regular noir, or at least those I have been used to, but I found this a refreshing change.<br/><br/>The dialogue at times was a little odd, and I found myself chuckling at parts I’m not sure if I was supposed to, but anyone sick of tried and tested should definitely give this a read. An almost Lynchian take on the noir genre, and that is no bad thing in my eyes.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2824450730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2824450730" />
    <a title="Litnigma Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97393889-litnigma-reviews"><img alt="Litnigma Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558117679p2/97393889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2824450730?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Litnigma Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Litnigma Reviews" href="/user/show/97393889-litnigma-reviews">Litnigma Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2824450730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9194074947099410153">Hairspray and Lighter is a throwback to the noir era trenchcoat-wearing gumshoe the likes of James Ellroy, but with a much darker and grittier edge. Eckerly is a fantastic protagonist and Jupes writing progressing in a fast and consistent manner, meaning there are plenty of hooks along along the way. A good and bad thing, as I did sleep in twice from reading too late the night before. Other than that though a fantastic read and I’ll be picking up each new J Jupes book when they’re released.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Iu9GeHGvj1P/5SfTglDI8HBaLVJMlshdpnYwO5SPqeAYyS+qyvFGO1jOk7J1pcIvpgXKmoIbRjr9CHaKWcxbeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eCuGTrwCiIcHfnO3eOy272wOqXSBgz3FNOcvYnZKC2tCDe+cB1xB76BVx9aPGbwwulFOvE8Os6JvmWnTuwn58Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17521631648570583410">J. Jupes writes pulp and dystopian novels and likes having a cover image in front of him before even thinking about the first word. He assembles books from notes written on the back of Mars Bar wrappers. Raised by a severe English playwright, Jupes can't stomach convention. His father made outlines. He doesn't. Jupes likes a sentence that smokes unfiltered cigarettes and flicks the butts into filt</span>
  <span id="freeText17521631648570583410" style="display:none">J. Jupes writes pulp and dystopian novels and likes having a cover image in front of him before even thinking about the first word. He assembles books from notes written on the back of Mars Bar wrappers. Raised by a severe English playwright, Jupes can't stomach convention. His father made outlines. He doesn't. Jupes likes a sentence that smokes unfiltered cigarettes and flicks the butts into filthy puddles just to hear them hiss. <br />"I type real fast with two fingers," he says, "like a two beaked woodpecker. I use a typewriter because I like pounding the keys and shoving the carriage over at the end of a line then ripping out the page and slapping it down on the Done Pile. I never went to writing school but I've been to the corner of Life and Anxiety and bought a pretzel. I have very few qualities people can relate to. I stays indoors and every night fall asleep in front of my little TV, waking myself snoring at about one or two, claw my way along the floor into bed and sleep on my bare mattress. I might pee a little bit in my sleep. I like waking up early to sit at the typewriter and warm my hands on a cup of Sanka. When the sun comes up, I make himself toast with butter and English marmalade and get depressed looking at my empty plate with the crumbs on it, like the world is nothing but toast and marmalade and crumbs. That’s when I’ll open the fridge and have a look see. I usually end up closing the door without taking anything out but might come back later and open the door again, or might not. And the J stands for Johnny."<br />Jupes also likes , as the English say, taking the piss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17521631648570583410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
